   <h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Legality of bitcoin by country or territory</h1> 
   <div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content"> 
    <div id="siteSub" class="noprint">
     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia
    </div> 
    <div id="contentSub"></div> 
    <div id="contentSub2"></div> 
    <div id="jump-to-nav"></div> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#searchInput">Jump to search</a> 
    <div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr">
     <div class="mw-parser-output">
      <p class="mw-empty-elt"> </p> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable plainlinks">
       This list is <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:WikiProject_Lists#Incomplete_lists" title="Wikipedia:WikiProject Lists">incomplete</a>; you can help by <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Legality_of_bitcoin_by_country_or_territory&amp;action=edit">adding missing items</a> with <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Reliable_sources" title="Wikipedia:Reliable sources">reliable sources</a>.
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Legal_status_of_bitcoin.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Legal_status_of_bitcoin.png/220px-Legal_status_of_bitcoin.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="96" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Legal_status_of_bitcoin.png/330px-Legal_status_of_bitcoin.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Legal_status_of_bitcoin.png/440px-Legal_status_of_bitcoin.png 2x" data-file-width="1425" data-file-height="625"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Legal_status_of_bitcoin.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Legal status of bitcoin 
         <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r981673959">.mw-parser-output .legend{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .legend-color{display:inline-block;min-width:1.25em;height:1.25em;line-height:1.25;margin:1px 0;text-align:center;border:1px solid black;background-color:transparent;color:black}.mw-parser-output .legend-text{}</style>
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#33cc66; color:black; -webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;<b>permissive</b> (legal to use bitcoin)
         </div> 
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#ffcc00; color:black; -webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;<b>contentious</b> (some legal restrictions on usage of bitcoin)
         </div> 
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#ec6dd5; color:black; -webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;<b>contentious</b> (interpretation of old laws, but bitcoin is not prohibited directly)
         </div> 
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#ff3333; color:black; -webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;<b>hostile</b> (full or partial prohibition)
         </div> 
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#808080; color:black; -webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;<b>no data</b>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The legal status of <a href="/wiki/Bitcoin" title="Bitcoin">bitcoin</a> (and related crypto instruments) varies substantially from state to state and is still undefined or changing in many of them.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> Whereas the majority of countries do not make the usage of bitcoin itself illegal, its status as money (or a commodity) varies, with differing regulatory implications.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>While some states have <i>explicitly</i> allowed its use and trade, others have banned or restricted it. Likewise, various government agencies, departments, and courts have classified bitcoins differently. While this article provides the legal status of bitcoin, regulations and bans that apply to this <a href="/wiki/Cryptocurrency" title="Cryptocurrency">cryptocurrency</a> likely extend to similar systems as well. </p> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r886046785">.mw-parser-output .toclimit-2 .toclevel-1 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-3 .toclevel-2 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-4 .toclevel-3 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-5 .toclevel-4 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-6 .toclevel-5 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-7 .toclevel-6 ul{display:none}</style>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Detail_by_union">Detail by union</span></h2> 
      <table class="wikitable sortable" style="text-align:left"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <th style="width:120px;"><b>Country or territory</b></th> 
         <th><b>Legality</b> </th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Flag_of_Europe.svg/23px-Flag_of_Europe.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Flag_of_Europe.svg/35px-Flag_of_Europe.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Flag_of_Europe.svg/45px-Flag_of_Europe.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="810" data-file-height="540">&nbsp;</span><a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a><span class="anchor" id="European_Union"></span> </td> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/File:Yes_check.svg" class="image"><img alt="Yes check.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/15px-Yes_check.svg.png" decoding="async" width="15" height="15" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/23px-Yes_check.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/30px-Yes_check.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="600"></a> Legal 
          <hr> <p>The European Union has passed no specific legislation relative to the status of bitcoin as a currency, but has stated that VAT/GST is not applicable to the conversion between traditional (fiat) currency and bitcoin. </p><p>VAT/GST and other taxes (such as income tax) still apply to transactions made using bitcoins for goods and services. <sup id="cite_ref-regulation_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-regulation-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap">:<span>European Union</span></sup> </p><p>In October 2015, the Court of Justice of the European Union ruled that "The exchange of traditional currencies for units of the 'bitcoin' virtual currency is exempt from VAT" and that "Member States must exempt, inter alia, transactions relating to 'currency, bank notes and coins used as <a href="/wiki/Legal_tender" title="Legal tender">legal tender</a><span style="padding-right:.15em;">'</span>", making bitcoin a currency as opposed to being a commodity.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> According to judges, the tax should not be charged because bitcoins should be treated as a means of payment.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> </p><p>According to the <a href="/wiki/European_Central_Bank" title="European Central Bank">European Central Bank</a>, traditional financial sector regulation is not applicable to bitcoin because it does not involve traditional financial actors.<sup id="cite_ref-ECB_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ECB-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>5</span></sup> Others in the EU have stated, however, that existing rules can be extended to include bitcoin and bitcoin companies.<sup id="cite_ref-EUPARANNEX_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EUPARANNEX-8">[8]</a></sup> </p><p>The European Central Bank classifies bitcoin as a convertible decentralized virtual currency.<sup id="cite_ref-ECB_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ECB-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>6</span></sup> In July 2014 the <a href="/wiki/European_Banking_Authority" title="European Banking Authority">European Banking Authority</a> advised European banks not to deal in virtual currencies such as bitcoin until a regulatory regime was in place.<sup id="cite_ref-EBA_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EBA-9">[9]</a></sup> </p><p>In 2016 the European Parliament's proposal to set up a taskforce to monitor virtual currencies to combat money laundering and terrorism, passed by 542 votes to 51, with 11 abstentions, has been sent to the European Commission for consideration.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> </p> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/G8_(forum)" class="mw-redirect" title="G8 (forum)">G7</a> </td> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/File:Yes_check.svg" class="image"><img alt="Yes check.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/15px-Yes_check.svg.png" decoding="async" width="15" height="15" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/23px-Yes_check.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/30px-Yes_check.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="600"></a> Legal 
          <hr> <p>In 2013 the <a href="/wiki/G7" class="mw-redirect" title="G7">G7</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Financial_Action_Task_Force" title="Financial Action Task Force">Financial Action Task Force</a> issued the following statement in guidelines which may be applicable to companies involved in transmitting bitcoin and other currencies, "Internet-based payment services that allow third party funding from anonymous sources may face an increased risk of [money laundering/terrorist financing]." They concluded that this may "pose challenges to countries in [anti-money laundering/counter terrorist financing] regulation and supervision".<sup id="cite_ref-fatf_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fatf-11">[11]</a></sup> </p> </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Africa">Africa</span></h3> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Northern_Africa">Northern Africa</span></h4> 
      <table class="wikitable sortable" style="text-align:left"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <th style="width:120px;"><b>Country or territory</b></th> 
         <th><b>Legality</b> </th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Flag_of_Algeria.svg/23px-Flag_of_Algeria.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Flag_of_Algeria.svg/35px-Flag_of_Algeria.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Flag_of_Algeria.svg/45px-Flag_of_Algeria.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600">&nbsp;</span><a href="/wiki/Algeria" title="Algeria">Algeria</a><span class="anchor" id="Algeria"></span> </td> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/File:X_mark.svg" class="image"><img alt="X mark.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/X_mark.svg/15px-X_mark.svg.png" decoding="async" width="15" height="17" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/X_mark.svg/23px-X_mark.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/X_mark.svg/30px-X_mark.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="525" data-file-height="600"></a> Illegal 
          <hr> <p>According to the "Journal Officiel" (28 December 2017): </p><p>Art. 117. — The purchase, sale, use, and holding of so-called virtual currency is prohibited. Virtual currency is that used by internet users via the web. It is characterized by the absence of physical support such as coins, notes, payments by cheque or credit card. Any breach of this provision is punishable in accordance with the laws and regulations in force.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-RCAWJune2018LOC_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RCAWJune2018LOC-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>82</span></sup> </p> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Flag_of_Egypt.svg/23px-Flag_of_Egypt.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Flag_of_Egypt.svg/35px-Flag_of_Egypt.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Flag_of_Egypt.svg/45px-Flag_of_Egypt.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600">&nbsp;</span><a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a><span class="anchor" id="Egypt"></span> </td> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/File:X_mark.svg" class="image"><img alt="X mark.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/X_mark.svg/15px-X_mark.svg.png" decoding="async" width="15" height="17" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/X_mark.svg/23px-X_mark.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/X_mark.svg/30px-X_mark.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="525" data-file-height="600"></a> Illegal 
          <hr> <p>"Egypt’s Dar al-Ifta, the primary Islamic legislator in Egypt, has issued a religious decree classifying commercial transactions in bitcoin as haram (prohibited under Islamic law)."<sup id="cite_ref-RCAWJune2018LOC_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RCAWJune2018LOC-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap">:<span>82</span></sup> </p> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Flag_of_Morocco.svg/23px-Flag_of_Morocco.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Flag_of_Morocco.svg/35px-Flag_of_Morocco.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Flag_of_Morocco.svg/45px-Flag_of_Morocco.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600">&nbsp;</span><a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a><span class="anchor" id="Morocco"></span> </td> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/File:X_mark.svg" class="image"><img alt="X mark.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/X_mark.svg/15px-X_mark.svg.png" decoding="async" width="15" height="17" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/X_mark.svg/23px-X_mark.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/X_mark.svg/30px-X_mark.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="525" data-file-height="600"></a> Illegal 
          <hr> <p>On 20 November 2017 the exchange office issued a public statement in which it declared, "The Office des Changes wishes to inform the general public that the transactions via virtual currencies constitute an infringement of the exchange regulations, liable to penalties and fines provided for by [existing laws] in force."<sup id="cite_ref-RCAWJune2018LOC_13-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RCAWJune2018LOC-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap">:<span>87</span></sup> </p><p>The following day, the monetary authorities also reacted in a statement issued jointly by the Ministry of Economy and Finance, Bank Al-Maghrib and the Moroccan Capital Market Authority (AMMC), warning against risks associated with bitcoin, which may be used "for illicit or criminal purposes, including money laundering and terrorist financing".<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> </p><p>On 19 December 2017, Abdellatif Jouahri, governor of Bank Al-Maghrib, said at a press conference held in Rabat during the last quarterly meeting of the Bank Al-Maghrib's Board of 2017 that bitcoin is not a currency but a "financial asset". He also warned of its dangers and called for a framework to be put in place for consumer protection.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> </p> </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Western_Africa">Western Africa</span></h4> 
      <table class="wikitable sortable" style="text-align:left"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <th style="width:120px;"><b>Country or territory</b></th> 
         <th><b>Legality</b> </th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Flag_of_Nigeria.svg/23px-Flag_of_Nigeria.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Flag_of_Nigeria.svg/35px-Flag_of_Nigeria.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Flag_of_Nigeria.svg/46px-Flag_of_Nigeria.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="600">&nbsp;</span><a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a><span class="anchor" id="Nigeria"></span> </td> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/File:Yes_check.svg" class="image"><img alt="Yes check.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/15px-Yes_check.svg.png" decoding="async" width="15" height="15" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/23px-Yes_check.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/30px-Yes_check.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="600"></a> Legal 
          <hr> <p>As of 17 January 2017, The Central Bank of Nigeria (CBN) has passed a circular to inform all Nigerian banks that bank transactions in bitcoin and other virtual currencies have been banned in Nigeria.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> </p><p>Later on, a committee was set up by the Central Bank of Nigeria (CBN) and the Nigeria Deposit Insurance Corporation (NDIC) to look into the possibility of the country adopting the technology driving bitcoin and other digital currencies – blockchain. The committee has submitted its report but "several sub-committees are still working on the issue" according to the Director, Banking &amp; Payments System Department at CBN, Mr. ‘Dipo Fatokun.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> </p> </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <h4><span id="East_.26_Central_Africa"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="East_&amp;_Central_Africa">East &amp; Central Africa</span></h4> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Southeast_Africa">Southeast Africa</span></h4> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Horn_of_Africa">Horn of Africa</span></h4> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Indian_Ocean_States">Indian Ocean States</span></h4> 
      <table class="wikitable sortable" style="text-align:left"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <th style="width:120px;"><b>Country or territory</b></th> 
         <th><b>Legality</b> </th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Flag_of_Mauritius.svg/23px-Flag_of_Mauritius.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Flag_of_Mauritius.svg/35px-Flag_of_Mauritius.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Flag_of_Mauritius.svg/45px-Flag_of_Mauritius.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600">&nbsp;</span><a href="/wiki/Mauritius" title="Mauritius">Mauritius</a><span class="anchor" id="Mauritius"></span> </td> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/File:Yes_check.svg" class="image"><img alt="Yes check.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/15px-Yes_check.svg.png" decoding="async" width="15" height="15" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/23px-Yes_check.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/30px-Yes_check.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="600"></a> Legal 
          <hr> <p>The Financial Services Commission of Mauritius considers cryptocurrencies to be regulated as a Digital Asset under the Financial Services Act 2007, and while it cautions investors they are not protected by any statutory compensation agreements, they are legal.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> </p> </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Southern_Africa">Southern Africa</span></h4> 
      <table class="wikitable sortable" style="text-align:left"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <th style="width:120px;"><b>Country or territory</b></th> 
         <th><b>Legality</b> </th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Flag_of_Angola.svg/23px-Flag_of_Angola.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Flag_of_Angola.svg/35px-Flag_of_Angola.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Flag_of_Angola.svg/45px-Flag_of_Angola.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600">&nbsp;</span><a href="/wiki/Angola" title="Angola">Angola</a><span class="anchor" id="Angola"></span> </td> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/File:Yes_check.svg" class="image"><img alt="Yes check.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/15px-Yes_check.svg.png" decoding="async" width="15" height="15" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/23px-Yes_check.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/30px-Yes_check.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="600"></a> Legal 
          <hr> <p>While government officials have advised against the use of Bitcoin, there is no legislation against it and it remains fully legal.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> </p> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Flag_of_South_Africa.svg/23px-Flag_of_South_Africa.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Flag_of_South_Africa.svg/35px-Flag_of_South_Africa.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Flag_of_South_Africa.svg/45px-Flag_of_South_Africa.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600">&nbsp;</span><a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a><span class="anchor" id="South_Africa"></span> </td> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/File:Yes_check.svg" class="image"><img alt="Yes check.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/15px-Yes_check.svg.png" decoding="async" width="15" height="15" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/23px-Yes_check.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/30px-Yes_check.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="600"></a> Legal 
          <hr> <p>In December 2014 the Reserve Bank of South Africa issued a position paper on virtual currencies whereby it declared that virtual currency had ‘no legal status or regulatory framework’.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> The South African Revenue Service classified bitcoin as an intangible asset.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> </p> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Flag_of_Namibia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Namibia.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Flag_of_Namibia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Namibia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Flag_of_Namibia.svg/45px-Flag_of_Namibia.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600">&nbsp;</span><a href="/wiki/Namibia" title="Namibia">Namibia</a><span class="anchor" id="Namibia"></span> </td> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/File:Yes_check.svg" class="image"><img alt="Yes check.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/15px-Yes_check.svg.png" decoding="async" width="15" height="15" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/23px-Yes_check.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/30px-Yes_check.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="600"></a> Legal 
          <hr> <p>In September 2017 the Bank of Namibia issued a position paper on virtual currencies entitled<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> wherein it declared cryptocurrency exchanges are not allowed and cryptocurrency cannot be accepted as payment for goods and services. </p> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Flag_of_Zimbabwe.svg/23px-Flag_of_Zimbabwe.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Flag_of_Zimbabwe.svg/35px-Flag_of_Zimbabwe.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Flag_of_Zimbabwe.svg/46px-Flag_of_Zimbabwe.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1260" data-file-height="630">&nbsp;</span><a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe" title="Zimbabwe">Zimbabwe</a><span class="anchor" id="Zimbabwe"></span> </td> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/File:Yes_check.svg" class="image"><img alt="Yes check.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/15px-Yes_check.svg.png" decoding="async" width="15" height="15" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/23px-Yes_check.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/30px-Yes_check.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="600"></a> Legal 
          <hr> <p>The Reserve Bank Of Zimbabwe is sceptical about bitcoin and has not officially permitted its use. On 5 April 2017 however, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.bitmari.com">BitMari</a>, a Pan-African Blockchain platform got licensed, through its banking partner, <a href="/wiki/Agricultural_Development_Bank_of_Zimbabwe" title="Agricultural Development Bank of Zimbabwe">AgriBank</a>, to operate in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> </p> </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Americas">Americas</span></h3> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="North_America">North America</span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/BitLicense" title="BitLicense">BitLicense</a>
      </div> 
      <table class="wikitable sortable" style="text-align:left"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <th style="width:120px;"><b>Country or territory</b></th> 
         <th><b>Legality</b> </th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Flag_of_Canada_%28Pantone%29.svg/23px-Flag_of_Canada_%28Pantone%29.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Flag_of_Canada_%28Pantone%29.svg/35px-Flag_of_Canada_%28Pantone%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Flag_of_Canada_%28Pantone%29.svg/46px-Flag_of_Canada_%28Pantone%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="600">&nbsp;</span><a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a><span class="anchor" id="Canada"></span> </td> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/File:Yes_check.svg" class="image"><img alt="Yes check.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/15px-Yes_check.svg.png" decoding="async" width="15" height="15" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/23px-Yes_check.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/30px-Yes_check.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="600"></a> Legal / <a href="/wiki/File:X_mark.svg" class="image"><img alt="X mark.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/X_mark.svg/15px-X_mark.svg.png" decoding="async" width="15" height="17" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/X_mark.svg/23px-X_mark.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/X_mark.svg/30px-X_mark.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="525" data-file-height="600"></a> Banking ban 
          <hr> <p>Companies dealing in virtual currencies must register with the Financial Transactions and Reports Analysis Centre of Canada (Fintrac), implement compliance programs, keep the required records, report suspicious or terrorist-related transactions, and determine if any of their customers are "politically exposed persons." </p><p>The law applies to non-Canadian virtual currency exchanges if they have Canadian customers. Banks may not open or maintain accounts or have a correspondent banking relationship with companies dealing in virtual currencies if that company is not registered with Fintrac. </p><p>Dealers in digital currency are regulated as money services businesses.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> </p><p>The Authorite des Marches Financiers, the regulator in the province of Quebec, has declared that some bitcoin related business models including exchanges and ATMs are regulated under its current MSB Act.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> </p><p>As of April 2018, the Bank of Montreal (BMO) announced that it would ban its credit and debit card customers from participating in cryptocurrency purchases with their cards.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> This is following another banking ban in Canada from Toronto Dominion (TD.)<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> </p> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1235" data-file-height="650">&nbsp;</span><a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a><span class="anchor" id="United_States"></span> </td> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/File:Yes_check.svg" class="image"><img alt="Yes check.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/15px-Yes_check.svg.png" decoding="async" width="15" height="15" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/23px-Yes_check.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/30px-Yes_check.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="600"></a> Legal 
          <hr> <p>The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_the_Treasury" title="United States Department of the Treasury">U.S. Treasury</a> classified bitcoin as a convertible decentralized virtual currency in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-JSC_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JSC-28">[28]</a></sup> The Commodity Futures Trading Commission, CFTC, classified bitcoin as a commodity in September 2015. Per IRS, bitcoin is taxed as a property.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> </p><p>Bitcoin was mentioned in a <a href="/wiki/U.S._Supreme_Court" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Supreme Court">U.S. Supreme Court</a> opinion (on Wisconsin Central Ltd. v. United States) regarding the changing definition of money on 21 June 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> </p><p>If money services businesses, including cryptocurrency exchanges, money transmitters, and anonymizing services (known as "mixers" or "tumblers") do a substantial amount of business in the U.S., they are required to </p> 
          <ul>
           <li>register with the U.S.<a href="/wiki/FinCEN" class="mw-redirect" title="FinCEN">FinCEN</a> as a money services business</li> 
           <li>design and enforce an anti-money laundering (AML) program, and</li> 
           <li>keep appropriate records and make reports to FinCEN, including Suspicious Activity Reports (SARs) and Currency Transaction Reports (CTRs)<sup id="cite_ref-fincen_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fincen-31">[31]</a></sup></li>
          </ul> <p>Seventeen other countries have similar AML requirements.<sup id="cite_ref-RCAWJune2018LOC_13-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RCAWJune2018LOC-13">[13]</a></sup> As of 2018 U.S. FinCEN receives more than 1,500 SARs per month involving cryptocurrencies.<sup id="cite_ref-fincen_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fincen-31">[31]</a></sup> </p><p>In September 2016, a federal judge ruled that "Bitcoins are funds within the plain meaning of that term".<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> </p> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Flag_of_Mexico.svg/23px-Flag_of_Mexico.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="13" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Flag_of_Mexico.svg/35px-Flag_of_Mexico.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Flag_of_Mexico.svg/46px-Flag_of_Mexico.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="980" data-file-height="560">&nbsp;</span><a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a><span class="anchor" id="Mexico"></span> </td> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/File:Yes_check.svg" class="image"><img alt="Yes check.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/15px-Yes_check.svg.png" decoding="async" width="15" height="15" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/23px-Yes_check.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/30px-Yes_check.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="600"></a> Legal 
          <hr> <p>Bitcoin is legal in Mexico as of 2017. It is to be regulated as a virtual asset by the FinTech Law.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> </p> </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table>

         <td><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Flag_of_Jamaica.svg/23px-Flag_of_Jamaica.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Flag_of_Jamaica.svg/35px-Flag_of_Jamaica.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Flag_of_Jamaica.svg/46px-Flag_of_Jamaica.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="600">&nbsp;</span><a href="/wiki/Jamaica" title="Jamaica">Jamaica</a><span class="anchor" id="Jamaica"></span> </td>

          <hr> <p>The Bank of Jamaica (BoJ), the national Central Bank, has publicly declared that it must create opportunities for the exploitation of technologies including cryptocurrencies. Accordingly, in 2017 the BoJ will be embarking on a campaign to build awareness of cryptocurrencies as part of increasing general financial literacy and understanding of cryptocurrencies. Indications are that early BoJ signals point to their general framework on "electronic retail payment service systems" possibly being brought to bear on initial cryptocurrencies considerations.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-regulation_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-regulation-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap">:<span>Jamaica</span></sup> </p> </td>

        <tr> 
         <td><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Flag_of_Argentina.svg/23px-Flag_of_Argentina.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="14" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Flag_of_Argentina.svg/35px-Flag_of_Argentina.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Flag_of_Argentina.svg/46px-Flag_of_Argentina.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="500">&nbsp;</span><a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a><span class="anchor" id="Argentina"></span> </td> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/File:Yes_check.svg" class="image"><img alt="Yes check.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/15px-Yes_check.svg.png" decoding="async" width="15" height="15" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/23px-Yes_check.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/30px-Yes_check.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="600"></a> Legal 
          <hr> <p>Bitcoins may be considered money, but not <a href="/wiki/Legal_tender" title="Legal tender">legal currency</a>. A bitcoin may be considered either a good or a thing under the Argentina's Civil Code, and transactions with bitcoins may be governed by the rules for the sale of goods under the Civil Code.<sup id="cite_ref-regulation_3-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-regulation-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap">:<span>Argentina</span></sup>. </p> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Flag_of_Bolivia.svg/22px-Flag_of_Bolivia.svg.png" decoding="async" width="22" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Flag_of_Bolivia.svg/34px-Flag_of_Bolivia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Flag_of_Bolivia.svg/44px-Flag_of_Bolivia.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1100" data-file-height="750">&nbsp;</span><a href="/wiki/Bolivia" title="Bolivia">Bolivia</a><span class="anchor" id="Bolivia"></span> </td>

          <hr> <p>Absolute ban.<sup id="cite_ref-RCAWJune2018LOC_13-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RCAWJune2018LOC-13">[13]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Central_Bank_of_Bolivia" title="Central Bank of Bolivia">Central Bank of Bolivia</a> issued a resolution banning bitcoin and any other currency not regulated by a country or economic zone in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-bol_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bol-40">[40]</a></sup> </p> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/05/Flag_of_Brazil.svg/22px-Flag_of_Brazil.svg.png" decoding="async" width="22" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/05/Flag_of_Brazil.svg/33px-Flag_of_Brazil.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/05/Flag_of_Brazil.svg/43px-Flag_of_Brazil.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="720" data-file-height="504">&nbsp;</span><a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a><span class="anchor" id="Brazil"></span> </td>

          <hr> <p>Not regulated, according to a 2014 statement by the <a href="/wiki/Central_Bank_of_Brazil" title="Central Bank of Brazil">Central Bank of Brazil</a> concerning cryptocurrencies, but is discouraged because of operational risks.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> In November 2017 this unregulated and discouraged status was reiterated by the Central Bank of Brazil.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> </p> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Flag_of_Chile.svg/23px-Flag_of_Chile.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Flag_of_Chile.svg/35px-Flag_of_Chile.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Flag_of_Chile.svg/45px-Flag_of_Chile.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1500" data-file-height="1000">&nbsp;</span><a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">Chile</a><span class="anchor" id="Chile"></span> </td> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/File:Yes_check.svg" class="image"><img alt="Yes check.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/15px-Yes_check.svg.png" decoding="async" width="15" height="15" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/23px-Yes_check.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/30px-Yes_check.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="600"></a> Legal 
          <hr> <p>There is no regulation on the use of bitcoins.<sup id="cite_ref-regulation_3-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-regulation-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap">:<span>Chile</span></sup> </p> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Flag_of_Colombia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Colombia.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Flag_of_Colombia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Colombia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Flag_of_Colombia.svg/45px-Flag_of_Colombia.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600">&nbsp;</span><a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a><span class="anchor" id="Colombia"></span> </td> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/File:Yes_check.svg" class="image"><img alt="Yes check.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/15px-Yes_check.svg.png" decoding="async" width="15" height="15" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/23px-Yes_check.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/30px-Yes_check.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="600"></a> Legal / <a href="/wiki/File:X_mark.svg" class="image"><img alt="X mark.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/X_mark.svg/15px-X_mark.svg.png" decoding="async" width="15" height="17" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/X_mark.svg/23px-X_mark.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/X_mark.svg/30px-X_mark.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="525" data-file-height="600"></a> Banking ban 
          <hr> <p>Financial institutions are not allowed to facilitate bitcoin transactions. The Superintendencia Financiera warned financial institutions in 2014 that they may not "protect, invest, broker, or manage virtual money operations".<sup id="cite_ref-RCAWJune2018LOC_13-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RCAWJune2018LOC-13">[13]</a></sup> </p> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Flag_of_Ecuador.svg/23px-Flag_of_Ecuador.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Flag_of_Ecuador.svg/35px-Flag_of_Ecuador.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Flag_of_Ecuador.svg/45px-Flag_of_Ecuador.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1440" data-file-height="960">&nbsp;</span><a href="/wiki/Ecuador" title="Ecuador">Ecuador</a><span class="anchor" id="Ecuador"></span> </td> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/File:X_mark.svg" class="image"><img alt="X mark.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/X_mark.svg/15px-X_mark.svg.png" decoding="async" width="15" height="17" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/X_mark.svg/23px-X_mark.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/X_mark.svg/30px-X_mark.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="525" data-file-height="600"></a> Illegal 
          <hr> <p>The Ecuadorian government has issued a ban on bitcoin and other digital currencies.<sup id="cite_ref-ecuador_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ecuador-43">[43]</a></sup> </p><p>The National Assembly of Ecuador banned bitcoins including other decentralized digital/crypto currencies, due to the establishment of a new state-run electronic money system. Ecuador's new project would be controlled by the government and tied directly to the local currency—the dollar. Users will be able to pay for select services and send money between individuals. This was slated to begin in mid-February 2015. "Electronic money is designed to operate and support the monetary scheme of dollarization," economist Diego Martinez, a delegate of the President of the Republic to the Board of Regulation and Monetary and Financial Policy.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> </p> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Flag_of_Venezuela.svg/23px-Flag_of_Venezuela.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Flag_of_Venezuela.svg/35px-Flag_of_Venezuela.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Flag_of_Venezuela.svg/45px-Flag_of_Venezuela.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600">&nbsp;</span><a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a> </td> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/File:Yes_check.svg" class="image"><img alt="Yes check.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/15px-Yes_check.svg.png" decoding="async" width="15" height="15" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/23px-Yes_check.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/30px-Yes_check.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="600"></a> Legal 
          <hr> <p>Bitcoin miners used to be arrested by law enforcement authorities, however in January 2018 Carlos Vargas, the government's cryptocurrency superintendent said “It is an activity that is now perfectly legal. We have had meetings with the Supreme Court so that people who have been victims of seizures and arrests in previous years will have charges dismissed.”<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> </p> </td>
        </tr>

      </table>

      <table class="wikitable sortable" style="text-align:left">

        <tr>

        <tr> 
         <td><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Flag_of_Cyprus.svg/23px-Flag_of_Cyprus.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Flag_of_Cyprus.svg/35px-Flag_of_Cyprus.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Flag_of_Cyprus.svg/45px-Flag_of_Cyprus.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600">&nbsp;</span><a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">Cyprus</a><span class="anchor" id="Cyprus"></span> </td> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/File:Yes_check.svg" class="image"><img alt="Yes check.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/15px-Yes_check.svg.png" decoding="async" width="15" height="15" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/23px-Yes_check.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/30px-Yes_check.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="600"></a> Legal 
          <hr> <p>The use of bitcoins is not regulated in Cyprus.<sup id="cite_ref-regulation_3-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-regulation-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap">:<span>Cyprus</span></sup> </p> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Russia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Russia.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Russia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Russia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Russia.svg/45px-Flag_of_Russia.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600">&nbsp;</span><a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a><span class="anchor" id="Russia"></span> </td> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/File:Yes_check.svg" class="image"><img alt="Yes check.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/15px-Yes_check.svg.png" decoding="async" width="15" height="15" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/23px-Yes_check.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/30px-Yes_check.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="600"></a> Legal to mine Bitcoin <a href="/wiki/File:X_mark.svg" class="image"><img alt="X mark.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/X_mark.svg/15px-X_mark.svg.png" decoding="async" width="15" height="17" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/X_mark.svg/23px-X_mark.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/X_mark.svg/30px-X_mark.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="525" data-file-height="600"></a> Banking ban 
          <hr> <p>As of November 2016, bitcoins are "not illegal" according to the Federal Tax Service of Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> Deputy Finance Minister of the Russian Federation Alexei Moiseev said in September 2017 it's "probably illegal" to accept cryptocurrency payments.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> However, bitcoin market sites are blocked, and court decisions state that bitcoin is a currency surrogate which is outlawed in the territory of the Russian Federation.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> </p><p>From the point of view of the current Russian legislation, cryptocurrency is a monetary substitute. According to article 27 of the Federal Law “On the Central Bank of the Russian Federation (Bank of Russia)”, the issue of monetary surrogates in the Russian Federation is prohibited.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> </p><p>The Central Bank of Russia and Rosfinmonitoring in their informational appeals have repeatedly warned Russian citizens that all operations with cryptocurrency are speculative and carry a high risk of loss of value. The Central Bank of Russia states that: "Most operations with cryptocurrencies are performed outside the legal regulation of both the Russian Federation and most other states. Cryptocurrencies are not guaranteed or provided by the Bank of Russia."<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> </p><p>A bill on digital financial assets was introduced in the State Duma on 20 March 2018. It defines cryptocurrency mining as "activities aimed at the creation of cryptocurrency with the purpose of receiving compensation in the form of cryptocurrency." and treats it as an "entrepreneurial activity subject to taxation if the miner exceeds the energy consumption limits established by the government for three months in a row." </p><p>In the bill, bitcoins are classified as property and are not considered legal tender. The exchange of cryptocurrency for rubles and foreign currency is allowed but only through licensed operators. The bill also provides a definition of a smart contract.<sup id="cite_ref-regulation_3-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-regulation-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap">:<span>Russia</span></sup> </p> </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table>

      <table class="wikitable sortable" style="text-align:left">

         <td><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Flag_of_the_United_Arab_Emirates.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_Arab_Emirates.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Flag_of_the_United_Arab_Emirates.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_Arab_Emirates.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Flag_of_the_United_Arab_Emirates.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_Arab_Emirates.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="600">&nbsp;</span><a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates" title="United Arab Emirates">United Arab Emirates</a><span class="anchor" id="United_Arab_Emirates"></span> </td> 
         <td>Contradictory information 
          <hr> <p>Absolute ban. According to the Library of Congress "Under article D.7.3 of the Regulatory Framework for Stored Values and an Electronic Payment System, issued by the Central Bank of the United Arab Emirates in January 2017, all transactions in “virtual currencies” (encompassing cryptocurrencies in Arabic) are prohibited."<sup id="cite_ref-RCAWJune2018LOC_13-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RCAWJune2018LOC-13">[13]</a></sup> </p><p>Nevertheless, on 13 February 2018 Dubai gold trader Regal RA DMCC became the first company in the Middle East to get a license to trade cryptocurrencies, the Dubai Multi Commodities Centre said.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> DMCC's website emphasizes the "cold storage" of cryptocurrencies and states "DMCC’s Crypto-commodities license is for Proprietary Trading in Crypto-commodities only. No initial coin offerings are permitted and no establishment of an exchange is permitted under this license."<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> </p> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Flag_of_Israel.svg/21px-Flag_of_Israel.svg.png" decoding="async" width="21" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Flag_of_Israel.svg/32px-Flag_of_Israel.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Flag_of_Israel.svg/41px-Flag_of_Israel.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1100" data-file-height="800">&nbsp;</span><a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a><span class="anchor" id="Israel"></span> </td> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/File:Yes_check.svg" class="image"><img alt="Yes check.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/15px-Yes_check.svg.png" decoding="async" width="15" height="15" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/23px-Yes_check.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/30px-Yes_check.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="600"></a> Legal 
          <hr> <p>As of 2017, the Israel Tax Authorities issued a statement saying that bitcoin and other cryptocurrencies would not fall under the legal definition of currency, and neither of that of a financial security, but of a taxable asset.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> Each time a bitcoin is sold, the seller would have to pay a capital gains tax of 25%. Miners, traders of bitcoins would be treated as businesses and would have to pay corporate income tax as well as charge a 17% VAT.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> </p> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Flag_of_Saudi_Arabia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Saudi_Arabia.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Flag_of_Saudi_Arabia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Saudi_Arabia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Flag_of_Saudi_Arabia.svg/45px-Flag_of_Saudi_Arabia.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600">&nbsp;</span><a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a><span class="anchor" id="Saudi_Arabia"></span> </td> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/File:Yes_check.svg" class="image"><img alt="Yes check.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/15px-Yes_check.svg.png" decoding="async" width="15" height="15" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/23px-Yes_check.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/30px-Yes_check.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="600"></a> Legal / <a href="/wiki/File:X_mark.svg" class="image"><img alt="X mark.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/X_mark.svg/15px-X_mark.svg.png" decoding="async" width="15" height="17" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/X_mark.svg/23px-X_mark.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/X_mark.svg/30px-X_mark.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="525" data-file-height="600"></a> Banking ban 
          <hr> <p>Financial institutions are warned from using bitcoin.<sup id="cite_ref-RCAWJune2018LOC_13-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RCAWJune2018LOC-13">[13]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabian_Monetary_Authority" class="mw-redirect" title="Saudi Arabian Monetary Authority">Saudi Arabian Monetary Authority</a> (SAMA) has warned from using bitcoin as it is high risk and its dealers will not be guaranteed any protection or rights.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> </p> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Flag_of_Jordan.svg/23px-Flag_of_Jordan.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Flag_of_Jordan.svg/35px-Flag_of_Jordan.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Flag_of_Jordan.svg/46px-Flag_of_Jordan.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="600">&nbsp;</span><a href="/wiki/Jordan" title="Jordan">Jordan</a><span class="anchor" id="Jordan"></span> </td>

          <hr> <p>The government of Jordan has issued a warning discouraging the use of bitcoin and other similar systems.<sup id="cite_ref-disco_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-disco-60">[60]</a></sup> </p><p>The Central Bank of Jordan prohibits banks, currency exchanges, financial companies, and payment service companies from dealing in bitcoins or other digital currencies.<sup id="cite_ref-jordantimes_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jordantimes-61">[61]</a></sup> While it warned the public of risks of bitcoins, and that they are not legal tender, bitcoins are still accepted by small businesses and merchants.<sup id="cite_ref-jordantimes_61-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jordantimes-61">[61]</a></sup> </p> </td>

          <hr> <p>Finance minister Arun Jaitley, in his budget speech on 1 February 2018, stated that the government will do everything to discontinue the use of bitcoin and other virtual currencies in India for criminal uses. He reiterated that India does not recognise them as legal tender and will instead encourage blockchain technology in payment systems. </p><p>"The government does not recognise cryptocurrency as legal tender or coin and will take all measures to eliminate the use of these cryptoassets in financing illegitimate activities or as part of the payments system," Jaitley said.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> </p><p>In early 2018 India's central bank, the <a href="/wiki/Reserve_Bank_of_India" title="Reserve Bank of India">Reserve Bank of India</a> (RBI) announced a ban on the sale or purchase of cryptocurrency for entities regulated by RBI.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> </p><p>In 2019, a petition has been filed by Internet and Mobile Association of India with the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_India" title="Supreme Court of India">Supreme Court of India</a> challenging the legality of cryptocurrencies and seeking a direction or order restraining their transaction.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> In March 2020, the Supreme Court of India passed the verdict, revoking the RBI ban on cryptocurrency trade.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> </p> </td>
        </tr>

Bank will not get involved if there is any dispute. They will not facilitate any transaction for it.          <td><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg/45px-Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600">&nbsp;</span><a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a> (PRC)<span class="anchor" id="China"></span> </td> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/File:Yes_check.svg" class="image"><img alt="Yes check.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/15px-Yes_check.svg.png" decoding="async" width="15" height="15" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/23px-Yes_check.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/30px-Yes_check.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="600"></a> Legal / <a href="/wiki/File:X_mark.svg" class="image"><img alt="X mark.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/X_mark.svg/15px-X_mark.svg.png" decoding="async" width="15" height="17" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/X_mark.svg/23px-X_mark.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/X_mark.svg/30px-X_mark.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="525" data-file-height="600"></a> Banking ban 
          <hr> <p>Financial institutions are not allowed to facilitate bitcoin transactions.<sup id="cite_ref-RCAWJune2018LOC_13-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RCAWJune2018LOC-13">[13]</a></sup> Regulation prohibits financial firms holding or trading cryptocurrencies.<sup id="cite_ref-EUPARANNEX_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EUPARANNEX-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap">:<span>China</span></sup> On 5 December 2013, <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Bank_of_China" title="People's Bank of China">People's Bank of China</a> (PBOC) made its first step in regulating bitcoin by prohibiting financial institutions from handling bitcoin transactions.<sup id="cite_ref-Bloomberd_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bloomberd-73">[73]</a></sup> </p><p>On 1 April 2014 PBOC ordered commercial banks and payment companies to close bitcoin trading accounts in two weeks.<sup id="cite_ref-wsj4-2014_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wsj4-2014-74">[74]</a></sup> </p><p>Cryptocurrency exchanges or trading platforms were effectively banned by regulation in September 2017 with 173 platforms closed down by July 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-LOC2018China_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LOC2018China-75">[75]</a></sup> </p><p>In early 2018 the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Bank_of_China" title="People's Bank of China">People's Bank of China</a> announced the <a href="/wiki/State_Administration_of_Foreign_Exchange" title="State Administration of Foreign Exchange">State Administration of Foreign Exchange</a> led by <a href="/wiki/Pan_Gongsheng" title="Pan Gongsheng">Pan Gongsheng</a> would crack down on bitcoin mining.<sup id="cite_ref-techcrunchBTC_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-techcrunchBTC-76">[76]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ChinaDaily20180105_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ChinaDaily20180105-77">[77]</a></sup> Many bitcoin mining operations in China had stopped operating by January 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-LOC2018China_75-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LOC2018China-75">[75]</a></sup> </p> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Flag_of_Hong_Kong.svg/23px-Flag_of_Hong_Kong.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Flag_of_Hong_Kong.svg/35px-Flag_of_Hong_Kong.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Flag_of_Hong_Kong.svg/45px-Flag_of_Hong_Kong.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600">&nbsp;</span><a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a><span class="anchor" id="Hong_Kong"></span> </td> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/File:Yes_check.svg" class="image"><img alt="Yes check.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/15px-Yes_check.svg.png" decoding="async" width="15" height="15" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/23px-Yes_check.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/30px-Yes_check.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="600"></a> Legal 
          <hr> <p>On 8 January 2014, the <a href="/wiki/Secretary_for_Financial_Services_and_the_Treasury" title="Secretary for Financial Services and the Treasury">Secretary for Financial Services and the Treasury</a> addressed bitcoin in the <a href="/wiki/Legislative_Council_of_Hong_Kong" title="Legislative Council of Hong Kong">Legislative Council</a> stating that "Hong Kong at present has no legislation directly regulating bitcoins and other virtual currencies of [a] similar kind. However, our existing laws (such as the Organised and Serious Crimes Ordinance) provide sanctions against unlawful acts involving bitcoins, such as fraud or money laundering."<sup id="cite_ref-regulation_3-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-regulation-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap">:<span>Hong Kong</span></sup> </p><p>On 16 November 2013, <a href="/wiki/Norman_Chan" title="Norman Chan">Norman Chan</a>, the chief executive of <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong_Monetary_Authority" title="Hong Kong Monetary Authority">Hong Kong Monetary Authority</a> (HKMA) said that bitcoin is only a virtual commodity. He also decided that bitcoin will not be regulated by HKMA. However, the authority will be closely watching the usage of bitcoin locally and its development overseas.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> </p> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9e/Flag_of_Japan.svg/23px-Flag_of_Japan.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9e/Flag_of_Japan.svg/35px-Flag_of_Japan.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9e/Flag_of_Japan.svg/45px-Flag_of_Japan.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600">&nbsp;</span><a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a><span class="anchor" id="Japan"></span> </td> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/File:Yes_check.svg" class="image"><img alt="Yes check.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/15px-Yes_check.svg.png" decoding="async" width="15" height="15" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/23px-Yes_check.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/30px-Yes_check.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="600"></a> Legal 
          <hr> <p>On 7 March 2014, the Japanese government, in response to a series of questions asked in the <a href="/wiki/National_Diet" title="National Diet">National Diet</a>, made a cabinet decision on the legal treatment of bitcoins in the form of answers to the questions.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> The decision did not see bitcoin as currency nor bond under the current Banking Act and Financial Instruments and Exchange Law, prohibiting banks and securities companies from dealing in bitcoins. The decision also acknowledges that there are no laws to unconditionally prohibit individuals or legal entities from receiving bitcoins in exchange for goods or services. Taxes may be applicable to bitcoins. </p><p>As of April 2017, cryptocurrency exchange businesses operating in Japan have been regulated by the Payment Services Act. Cryptocurrency exchange businesses have to be registered, keep records, take security measures, and take measures to protect customers. The law on cryptocurrency transactions must comply with the anti-money laundering law; and measures to protect users investors. The Payment Services Act defines “cryptocurrency” as a property value. The Act also states that cryptocurrency is limited to property values that are stored electronically on electronic devices, not a legal tender.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> </p> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Flag_of_South_Korea.svg/23px-Flag_of_South_Korea.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Flag_of_South_Korea.svg/35px-Flag_of_South_Korea.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Flag_of_South_Korea.svg/45px-Flag_of_South_Korea.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600">&nbsp;</span><a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">South Korea</a><span class="anchor" id="South_Korea"></span> </td> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/File:Yes_check.svg" class="image"><img alt="Yes check.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/15px-Yes_check.svg.png" decoding="async" width="15" height="15" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/23px-Yes_check.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/30px-Yes_check.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="600"></a> Legal 
          <hr> <p>Minors and all foreigners are prohibited from trading cryptocurrencies. Adult South Koreans may trade on registered exchanges using <i>real name</i> accounts at a bank where the exchange also has an account. Both the bank and the exchange are responsible for verifying the customer's identity and enforcing other anti-money-laundering provisions.<sup id="cite_ref-LOCJune2018_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LOCJune2018-81">[81]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> </p> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Flag_of_the_Republic_of_China.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_Republic_of_China.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Flag_of_the_Republic_of_China.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_Republic_of_China.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Flag_of_the_Republic_of_China.svg/45px-Flag_of_the_Republic_of_China.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600">&nbsp;</span><a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a><span class="anchor" id="Taiwan"></span> </td> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/File:Yes_check.svg" class="image"><img alt="Yes check.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/15px-Yes_check.svg.png" decoding="async" width="15" height="15" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/23px-Yes_check.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/30px-Yes_check.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="600"></a> Legal / <a href="/wiki/File:X_mark.svg" class="image"><img alt="X mark.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/X_mark.svg/15px-X_mark.svg.png" decoding="async" width="15" height="17" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/X_mark.svg/23px-X_mark.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/X_mark.svg/30px-X_mark.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="525" data-file-height="600"></a> Banking ban 
          <hr> <p>Financial institutions are not allowed to facilitate bitcoin transactions.<sup id="cite_ref-RCAWJune2018LOC_13-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RCAWJune2018LOC-13">[13]</a></sup> Regulators have warned the public that bitcoin does not have legal protection, "as the currency is not issued by any monetary authority and is therefore not entitled to legal claims or guarantee of conversion".<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> </p><p>Financial institutions have been warned by regulators that necessary regulatory actions may be taken if they use bitcoin.<sup id="cite_ref-regulation_3-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-regulation-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap">:<span>Taiwan</span></sup> </p><p>On 31 December 2013, <a href="/wiki/Financial_Supervisory_Commission_(Republic_of_China)" class="mw-redirect" title="Financial Supervisory Commission (Republic of China)">Financial Supervisory Commission (Republic of China)</a> (FSC) and CBC issued a joint statement which warns against the use of bitcoin. It is stated that bitcoin remains highly volatile, highly speculative, and is not entitled to legal claims or guarantee of conversion.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> </p><p>On 5 January 2014, FSC chairman <a href="/wiki/Tseng_Ming-chung" title="Tseng Ming-chung">Tseng Ming-chung</a> stated that FSC will not allow the installation of bitcoin ATM in Taiwan because bitcoin is not a currency and it should not be accepted by individuals and banks as payment.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> </p> </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table>

          <hr> <p>The National Bank of Cambodia (NBC), has "asked banks in Cambodia not to allow people to conduct transactions with cryptocurrencies."<sup id="cite_ref-RCAWJune2018LOC_13-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RCAWJune2018LOC-13">[13]</a></sup> </p> </td>

          <hr> <p>On 7 December 2017, <a href="/wiki/Bank_Indonesia" title="Bank Indonesia">Bank Indonesia</a>, the country's central bank, issued a regulation banning the use of cryptocurrencies including bitcoin as payment tools starting 1 January 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-RCAWJune2018LOC_13-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RCAWJune2018LOC-13">[13]</a></sup> </p> </td>

         <td><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Flag_of_Malaysia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Malaysia.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Flag_of_Malaysia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Malaysia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Flag_of_Malaysia.svg/46px-Flag_of_Malaysia.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="600">&nbsp;</span><a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a><span class="anchor" id="Malaysia"></span> </td>

          <hr> <p>On 4 November 2013, <a href="/wiki/Bank_Negara_Malaysia" class="mw-redirect" title="Bank Negara Malaysia">Bank Negara Malaysia</a> (BNM) met with local bitcoin proponents to learn more about the currency but did not comment at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> BNM issued a statement on 6 January 2014 that bitcoin is not recognised as a legal tender in <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a>. The central bank will not regulate bitcoin operations at the moment and users should aware of the risks associated with bitcoin usage.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-regulation_3-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-regulation-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap">:<span>Malaysia</span></sup> </p> </td>
        </tr>

         <td><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Flag_of_the_Philippines.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_Philippines.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Flag_of_the_Philippines.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_Philippines.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Flag_of_the_Philippines.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_Philippines.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="600">&nbsp;</span><a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a><span class="anchor" id="Philippines"></span> </td>
